### **Me** - 2018-08-30 20:21:49

I'm thinking about adding the concept of bonus days. These are for when I have my kids or want to go in a date. On these days I'll get double my DA.

### **Chris Duncan** - 2018-08-30 20:30:09

 I think dates should be a budgeted account separate from your DA.

Days with kids I could see being a little more flexible but I think it would be better to account that in for your total DA and adjust it to be more each day. Knowing that you will have to be in buffer by the time your kids come. 

I think the important thing if you do bonus days is to ONLY spend that money on kids/date. If your date goes cheaper, it shouldn’t be an excuse to spend that money elsewhere like you would for your typical DA

### **Me** - 2018-08-30 20:31:11

Hmm. Why not get to keep it?

### **Chris Duncan** - 2018-08-30 20:33:50

I mean, it goes against the spirit of future money. You have an event where it was “necessary” to have more money, but you found a way to do it cheaper. So it shows you didn’t really need that bonus. 

### **Chris Duncan** - 2018-08-30 20:35:38

### **Me** - 2019-03-13 00:57:51

How does lower standards connect to hypocrisy?

### **Chris Duncan** - 2019-03-13 01:02:54

For example, if I say to myself “i must do ‘x’”, but don’t say you must do it, isn’t that a form of hypocrisy? I’m not saying it’s bad. (And maybe not even hypocrisy really).

But if there’s room for that, is there room for holding people at a higher standard “it’s okay for me to do ‘x’, but not you”?

And lastly, the other view is to hold everyone to my standard, “Everyone (including myself), should be doing ‘x’”

### **Chris Duncan** - 2019-03-13 01:03:25

Unintentionally laid out ‘xxx’ 😁

### **Me** - 2019-03-13 01:03:34

Haha

### **Chris Duncan** - 2019-03-13 01:12:18

We’ll bring the ski trip for an example

A few different scenarios:

What if I kept skiing and you stopped

1) I could judge you for not continuing to ski even though I would be okay with doing the same thing personally. Would this be hypocritical?

2) Or what if I didn’t judge you, even though I would judge myself? Would this be hypocritical?

### **Me** - 2020-10-28 15:07:49

Life Lessons from WoW Classic

Consistent work and good strategy got me Epic loot and my Epic Mount.
- I'm capable of getting the best. I'm worthy.

Silence, patience, and rooting for others is how you cope with missing out on loot. Disappointment is inevitable but complaining is not.
- Loot desire is the same as sexual desire. Only the fool complains about not getting loot.

Teamwork is how you put dungeons on farm. How you reach difficult goals you couldn't do alone.
- I've never really enjoyed organized sports. Being in a competitive guild had taught me to value teamwork more.

Silent endurance helps you cope with difficult people. Guild members can be challenging and a lot like sport locker rooms.
- I'm easily offended. In WoW, I've often run across people who love to stir the pot and cause drama. I've learned to be patient and endure the drama. My moment will come. It's often not about me.

### **Me** - 2021-03-17 20:11:42

“Any sort of personal best performance will involve discomfort because you’re pushing yourself past what you’ve done before,” Aoyagi says. “Expecting discomfort allows us to accept and even embrace it as a sign that things are going right rather than things are going wrong.”

### **Me** - 2021-03-17 20:13:41

Aoyagi explains that when we accept the discomfort, two really important things happen: First, we can dedicate our brainpower to accomplishing the physical task at hand—setting the pace and breathing, rather than fighting the uncomfortable feelings. Second, we avoid piling extra pain on top by judgment (“If I were fit, I wouldn’t be feeling this.”), worrying about it (“If I feel like this already, there is no way I’m going to be able to finish.”), or catastrophizing it (“If I feel like this now I might as well quit because I’m not going to get the results I want.”).

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 16:42:18

Just watched Peter Attia on fasting.

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 16:42:28

Big issue is muscle loss.

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 16:43:26

He is emphasizing exercise.

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 16:53:15

I may not do fasting after watching all this.

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 17:06:02

He basically argues that it really hard to get sufficient protein while intermittent fasting. He believes it’s the most important macro nutrient and that while losing weight we should strive to keep our lean muscle mass.

### **Me** - 2023-09-24 17:07:43

In order of most difficult diets he ranks them: calorie counting > dietary restriction > time restriction. All have disadvantages. He suggests that calorie counting is the most direct but also the hardest to maintain.

### **Me** - 2025-11-29 12:38:09

This may be the key insight to turn your desire to have a successful business into a reality.

When I ask myself, “Do I know what people want so much they are willing to pay for?” I’d like to believe with all my experience and learning that the answer is ‘yes’, but more truthfully, I think the answer is often ‘no’.

In fact, generally, I don’t even start with that question. Most businesses start as a solution in search of a problem or an audience. This usually leads to failure.

Probably, a better approach is to collect people’s hopes and problems, in search of what people want more than the little money they have.

It’s also true that natural gifting creates the guardrails for the search. I’m reminded of pre-movie-release interviews.
